  └ firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pwm_capture/main.c (+141 -0)
      1 +/*
      2 + * STM32F103RCT6 — PB8/PB9 PWM capture mailbox test
      3 + *
      4 + * Observable behaviour:
      5 + *   - PB8 drives a software PWM waveform
      6 + *   - PB9 samples the looped-back waveform
      7 + *   - TIM2 free-runs at 1 MHz to measure high time and period
      8 + *   - PASS when duty and period stay inside the expected windows
      9 + *   - detail0 = ((period_us << 16) | high_us)
     10 + *
     11 + * Wiring required: PB8 -> PB9
     12 + * Mailbox address: 0x2000BC00
     13 + */
     14 +
     15 +#include <stdint.h>
     16 +
     17 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR 0x2000BC00u
     18 +#include "ael_mailbox.h"
     19 +
     20 +#define RCC_BASE        0x40021000U
     21 +#define RCC_APB2ENR     (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x18U))
     22 +#define RCC_APB1ENR     (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x1CU))
     23 +
     24 +#define GPIOB_BASE      0x40010C00U
     25 +#define GPIOB_CRH       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x04U))
     26 +#define GPIOB_IDR       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x08U))
     27 +#define GPIOB_ODR       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x0CU))
     28 +
     29 +#define TIM2_BASE       0x40000000U
     30 +#define TIM2_CR1        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x00U))
     31 +#define TIM2_PSC        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x28U))
     32 +#define TIM2_ARR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x2CU))
     33 +#define TIM2_CNT        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x24U))
     34 +#define TIM2_EGR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x14U))
     35 +
     36 +#define TIM_CR1_CEN       (1U << 0)
     37 +
     38 +#define ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT  0xC201U
     39 +#define ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT  0xC202U
     40 +#define ERR_PERIOD_RANGE  0xC203U
     41 +#define ERR_DUTY_RANGE    0xC204U
     42 +
     43 +static void delay_us(uint32_t us)
     44 +{
     45 +    uint32_t start = TIM2_CNT;
     46 +    while ((uint32_t)(TIM2_CNT - start) < us) {}
     47 +}
     48 +
     49 +static uint32_t read_pb9(void)
     50 +{
     51 +    return (GPIOB_IDR >> 9) & 1U;
     52 +}
     53 +
     54 +static uint32_t wait_for_level(uint32_t level, uint32_t timeout_us)
     55 +{
     56 +    while (timeout_us--) {
     57 +        if (read_pb9() == level) {
     58 +            return 1U;
     59 +        }
     60 +        delay_us(1U);
     61 +    }
     62 +    return 0U;
     63 +}
     64 +
     65 +int main(void)
     66 +{
     67 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= (1U << 3);
     68 +    RCC_APB1ENR |= (1U << 0);
     69 +
     70 +    /*
     71 +     * PB8: output push-pull 50 MHz -> CRH[3:0] = 0x3
     72 +     * PB9: input pull-down         -> CRH[7:4] = 0x8, ODR9 = 0
     73 +     */
     74 +    GPIOB_CRH &= ~0xFFU;
     75 +    GPIOB_CRH |=  0x83U;
     76 +    GPIOB_ODR &= ~((1U << 9) | (1U << 8));
     77 +
     78 +    TIM2_PSC = 7U;
     79 +    TIM2_ARR = 0xFFFFFFFFU;
     80 +    TIM2_EGR = 1U;
     81 +    TIM2_CNT = 0U;
     82 +    TIM2_CR1 = TIM_CR1_CEN;
     83 +
     84 +    ael_mailbox_init();
     85 +
     86 +    GPIOB_ODR &= ~(1U << 8);
     87 +    if (!wait_for_level(0U, 5000U)) {
     88 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT, 0U);
     89 +        while (1) {}
     90 +    }
     91 +
     92 +    uint32_t rise1 = 0U;
     93 +    uint32_t fall1 = 0U;
     94 +    uint32_t rise2 = 0U;
     95 +    uint32_t last_state = 0U;
     96 +
     97 +    for (uint32_t cycles = 0U; cycles < 32U; cycles++) {
     98 +        GPIOB_ODR |= (1U << 8);
     99 +        delay_us(400U);
    100 +        uint32_t state = read_pb9();
    101 +        if (state == 1U && last_state == 0U && rise1 == 0U) {
    102 +            rise1 = TIM2_CNT;
    103 +        }
    104 +        last_state = state;
    105 +
    106 +        GPIOB_ODR &= ~(1U << 8);
    107 +        delay_us(600U);
    108 +        state = read_pb9();
    109 +        if (state == 0U && last_state == 1U && rise1 != 0U && fall1 == 0U) {
    110 +            fall1 = TIM2_CNT;
    111 +        } else if (state == 1U && last_state == 0U && fall1 != 0U) {
    112 +            rise2 = TIM2_CNT;
    113 +            break;
    114 +        }
    115 +        last_state = state;
    116 +    }
    117 +
    118 +    if (rise1 == 0U || fall1 == 0U || rise2 == 0U) {
    119 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT, 0U);
    120 +        while (1) {}
    121 +    }
    122 +
    123 +    uint32_t high_us = fall1 - rise1;
    124 +    uint32_t period_us = rise2 - rise1;
    125 +    AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (period_us << 16) | (high_us & 0xFFFFU);
    126 +
    127 +    if (period_us < 800U || period_us > 1300U) {
    128 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_PERIOD_RANGE, period_us);
    129 +        while (1) {}
    130 +    }
    131 +    if (high_us < 250U || high_us > 550U) {
    132 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_DUTY_RANGE, high_us);
    133 +        while (1) {}
    134 +    }
    135 +
    136 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    137 +    while (1) {
    138 +        delay_us(1000U);
    139 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    140 +    }
    141 +}

     65 +- dma: `AEL_UART_DMA A1 B2 C3 D4 55 66 77 88`
     66 +- banner: `AEL_READY STM32F103RCT6 UART`
     67 +
     68 +## Key Findings
     69 +
     70 +1. `PB8 -> PB9` is now usable again after wiring repair.
     71 +   The dedicated `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe` now passes and the repaired wire
     72 +   is good enough to carry both `capture` and `pwm_capture`.
     73 +
     74 +2. The original `exti_trigger` route was a bad canonical choice for this bench.
     75 +   The suite now uses `PA0 -> PA1` for `EXTI1`, which reuses an already-proven
     76 +   wire and avoids depending on the repaired timer path for EXTI coverage.
     77 +
     78 +3. `uart_multibyte` and `uart_dma` should remain host-observed on this fixture.
     79 +   The current DAPLink setup exposes `PA9/PA10` as an external UART path, not a
     80 +   board-local `PA9 -> PA10` loopback path. The suite therefore validates
     81 +   `USART1 TX` and `DMA1 -> USART1 TX` honestly through UART observation plus
     82 +   mailbox PASS, rather than pretending board-local RX loopback exists.
     83 +
     84 +4. `OpenOCD sleep` uses milliseconds, not seconds.
     85 +   Early mailbox reads were caused by using `sleep 2` and `sleep 5` when the
     86 +   intended waits were 2 s and 5 s. On this path, use `sleep 2000` and similar.
     87 +
     88 +5. This DAPLink probe should be treated as single-session only.
     89 +   Parallel OpenOCD sessions intermittently destabilize the probe and cause
     90 +   `CMSIS-DAP failed to connect in mode (1)`. Serialized sessions are stable.
     91 +
     92 +## Candidate Status
     93 +
     94 +The suite is now strong enough to keep as a staged candidate with broad live
     95 +coverage, but this closeout does not promote it to `golden` yet.
     96 +
     97 +Reason:
     98 +
     99 +- `stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual` is still a human-observed visual proof and
    100 +  was not machine-verified in this closeout.
    101 +- the formal board/instrument metadata still points at legacy/non-DAPLink paths
    102 +  and has not yet been updated to a canonical local DAPLink/OpenOCD execution
    103 +  route.
    104 +
    105 +## Recommended Next Step
    106 +
    107 +Before promoting `stm32f103rct6` to `golden`:
    108 +
    109 +1. formalize the canonical local DAPLink/OpenOCD execution path in metadata
    110 +2. rerun the full candidate suite on that canonical path
    111 +3. explicitly confirm `pc7_blinky_visual`
    112 +4. then update lifecycle/labels from `candidate` to `golden`

  └ docs/skills/stm32f103rct6_daplink_live_validation_skill_2026-03-31.md (+112 -0)
      1 +# STM32F103RCT6 DAPLink Live Validation Skill
      2 +
      3 +## Use When
      4 +
      5 +Use this skill when validating `STM32F103RCT6` firmware on the repaired local
      6 +DAPLink fixture using direct `OpenOCD` access instead of the repo's older bench
      7 +adapters.
      8 +
      9 +Fixture shape:
     10 +
     11 +- DAPLink SWD
     12 +- DAPLink UART `<->` `PA9/PA10`
     13 +- `PC7 -> LED`
     14 +- `PB0 -> PB1`
     15 +- `PB8 -> PB9`
     16 +- `PA0 -> PA1`
     17 +- `PB15 -> PB14`
     18 +
     19 +## Core Rules
     20 +
     21 +1. Use `OpenOCD` with:
     22 +
     23 +   - `-f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg`
     24 +   - `-c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50"`
     25 +   - `-f target/stm32f1x.cfg`
     26 +
     27 +2. Do not run multiple `OpenOCD` sessions in parallel against this DAPLink.
     28 +   The probe can fall into:
     29 +
     30 +   - `CMSIS-DAP failed to connect in mode (1)`
     31 +
     32 +   if two sessions race.
     33 +
     34 +3. `sleep` inside `OpenOCD` uses milliseconds.
     35 +
     36 +   Examples:
     37 +
     38 +   - `sleep 2000` = 2 seconds
     39 +   - `sleep 500` = 0.5 seconds
     40 +
     41 +4. Before trusting `PB8 -> PB9` timer-path tests, run the probe firmware once:
     42 +
     43 +   - `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe`
     44 +
     45 +5. On this fixture, UART multibyte and UART DMA should be host-observed TX
     46 +   proofs, not fake board-local loopback tests.
     47 +
     48 +## Working Flash Pattern
     49 +
     50 +```bash
     51 +openocd \
     52 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
     53 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
     54 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
     55 +  -c "program <firmware>.elf verify reset exit"
     56 +```
     57 +
     58 +## Working Mailbox Read Pattern
     59 +
     60 +```bash
     61 +openocd \
     62 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
     63 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
     64 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
     65 +  -c init \
     66 +  -c "reset run" \
     67 +  -c "sleep 2000" \
     68 +  -c halt \
     69 +  -c "mdw 0x2000BC00 4" \
     70 +  -c exit
     71 +```
     72 +
     73 +Expected PASS shape:
     74 +
     75 +- `magic = 0xAE100001`
     76 +- `status = 0x00000002`
     77 +- `error_code = 0`
     78 +
     79 +## Bench-Specific Lessons
     80 +
     81 +### EXTI
     82 +
     83 +Do not anchor `exti_trigger` to `PB8/PB9` on this fixture. Reuse the already
     84 +validated `PA0 -> PA1` path and validate `EXTI1`.
     85 +
     86 +### Capture / PWM
     87 +
     88 +Use the repaired `PB8 -> PB9` wire for timer-edge tests. A dedicated
     89 +`pb8_pb9_probe` should PASS before trusting:
     90 +
     91 +- `stm32f103rct6_capture_mailbox`
     92 +- `stm32f103rct6_pwm_capture`
     93 +
     94 +### UART
     95 +
     96 +Use the DAPLink serial path as the canonical UART proof path:
     97 +
     98 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_banner`
     99 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_multibyte`
    100 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_dma`
    101 +
    102 +Representative expected strings:
    103 +
    104 +- `AEL_READY STM32F103RCT6 UART`
    105 +- `AEL_UART_MB 55 AA 12 34`
    106 +- `AEL_UART_DMA A1 B2 C3 D4 55 66 77 88`
    107 +
    108 +## Outcome Pattern
    109 +
    110 +If all non-visual tests pass but metadata still points at a legacy instrument
    111 +path, record the suite as a strongly validated `candidate`, not `golden`, until
    112 +the canonical board/instrument metadata is corrected.

• 是的，现有代码确实在驱动 PC7。

  证据：

  - firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual/main.c
      - 把 GPIOC 的 PC7 配成输出
      - 用 GPIOC_ODR ^= (1u << 7) 翻转 PC7
  - tests/plans/stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual.json
      - dut_signal: "PC7"
      - notes 里也明确写了 onboard LED on PC7

  所以如果你把：

  - PC6 <-> PC7

  连起来，我完全可以不用纯目视，改成：

  - PC7 继续作为输出
  - PC6 作为输入检测
  - 做一个 mailbox/self-check 版 LED proof

  这样会比现在的 visual_smoke 更好，因为能机器验证，不依赖人眼。

  最小实现我建议是：

  - 保留现在的 pc7_blinky_visual 不删
  - 另外新增一个：
      - stm32f103rct6_pc7_pc6_led_probe
  - 行为：
      - PC7 每隔固定时间翻转
      - PC6 轮询读取高低变化
      - 看到足够次数的有效翻转就 PASS

  这会把当前 Stage 0 里最弱的一项变强。

  你把 PC6 <-> PC7 接好以后，我下一步就直接实现并验证它。

     1 +#include <stdint.h>
     2 +
     3 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR 0x2000BC00u
     4 +#include "../stm32f103rct6/ael_mailbox.h"
     5 +
     6 +#define RCC_BASE    0x40021000u
     7 +#define RCC_APB2ENR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x18u))
     8 +#define RCC_IOPCEN  (1u << 4)
     9 +
    10 +#define GPIOC_BASE  0x40011000u
    11 +#define GPIOC_CRH   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x04u))
    12 +#define GPIOC_IDR   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x08u))
    13 +#define GPIOC_ODR   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x0Cu))
    14 +
    15 +#define SYSTICK_BASE 0xE000E010u
    16 +#define SYST_CSR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x00u))
    17 +#define SYST_RVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x04u))
    18 +#define SYST_CVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x08u))
    19 +
    20 +#define SYST_CSR_ENABLE     (1u << 0)
    21 +#define SYST_CSR_CLKSOURCE  (1u << 2)
    22 +#define SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG  (1u << 16)
    23 +
    24 +#define ERR_HIGH_MISS 0xE701u
    25 +#define ERR_LOW_MISS  0xE702u
    26 +
    27 +int main(void)
    28 +{
    29 +    uint32_t toggles = 0u;
    30 +    uint32_t high_seen = 0u;
    31 +    uint32_t low_seen = 0u;
    32 +
    33 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= RCC_IOPCEN;
    34 +
    35 +    /*
    36 +     * PC6: input pull-down -> CRH[11:8] = 0x8, ODR6 = 0
    37 +     * PC7: output push-pull 2 MHz -> CRH[15:12] = 0x2
    38 +     */
    39 +    GPIOC_CRH &= ~(0xFFu << 8u);
    40 +    GPIOC_CRH |=  (0x28u << 8u);
    41 +    GPIOC_ODR &= ~((1u << 6u) | (1u << 7u));
    42 +
    43 +    SYST_RVR = 7999u;
    44 +    SYST_CVR = 0u;
    45 +    SYST_CSR = SYST_CSR_CLKSOURCE | SYST_CSR_ENABLE;
    46 +
    47 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    48 +
    49 +    while (1) {
    50 +        if ((SYST_CSR & SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG) == 0u) {
    51 +            continue;
    52 +        }
    53 +
    54 +        toggles++;
    55 +        GPIOC_ODR ^= (1u << 7u);
    56 +
    57 +        if (GPIOC_ODR & (1u << 7u)) {
    58 +            if ((GPIOC_IDR & (1u << 6u)) == 0u) {
    59 +                ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_HIGH_MISS, toggles);
    60 +                while (1) {}
    61 +            }
    62 +            high_seen++;
    63 +        } else {
    64 +            if (GPIOC_IDR & (1u << 6u)) {
    65 +                ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_LOW_MISS, toggles);
    66 +                while (1) {}
    67 +            }
    68 +            low_seen++;
    69 +        }
    70 +
    71 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (high_seen << 16u) | low_seen;
    72 +        if (high_seen >= 4u && low_seen >= 4u) {
    73 +            ael_mailbox_pass();
    74 +            while (1) {
    75 +                if ((SYST_CSR & SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG) == 0u) {
    76 +                    continue;
    77 +                }
    78 +                AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    79 +            }
    80 +        }
    81 +    }
    82 +}

• 查过了，现有 blinky 代码确实是在驱动 PC7：

  - firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual/main.c
  - tests/plans/stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual.json

  我也按你的想法做了一个新的 PC7 -> PC6 机器验证 probe，并实机跑了：

  - 新增 target: firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pc7_pc6_led_probe/main.c
  - 新增 plan: tests/plans/stm32f103rct6_pc7_pc6_led_probe.json
  - 提交: f16dc22 feat: add stm32f103rct6 pc7 pc6 led probe

  结果是 FAIL，mailbox 读到：

  - ae100001 00000003 0000e702 00000002

  含义是：

  - status = FAIL
  - error_code = 0xE702，也就是我定义的 ERR_LOW_MISS
  - detail0 = 2

  这说明：

  - PC7 在代码里确实在翻转
  - 但 PC6 没有稳定读到对应的低电平变化
  - 所以“LED 不亮”现在不能简单归因于代码没驱动 PC7

  更像的情况是：

  - PC7 板上挂的 LED/外围电路不是你以为的那种连接
  - 或 PC7 这根线上还有别的板级负载/上拉
  - 或 silk/原理与实际不一致

  所以当前结论是：

  - code is using PC7: 是
  - PC6 <- PC7 这个验证法：我已经试了，但当前没有证明出一个干净可读的 PC7 数字波形

  如果你要继续，我建议下一步二选一：

  1. 你给我 LED 那一侧的实际原理/照片，我判断 PC7 是不是低有效、经过三极管、或并不是直连 LED
  2. 我再做一个更底层的 PC7 static high/low probe，分别停在高和低，用 SWD 读 GPIOC_ODR/IDR，把“代码输出”和“板上电平”进一步拆开


› 有可能PC7这端的硬件上出什么问题,如果把PC8、PC9连起来,你重新做这个实验,看能不能成功,就是PC8、PC9互相验证。


• 我先不动现有 PC7 结论，直接做一个新的 PC8 -> PC9 probe。这样能快速判断是不是 GPIOC 这组口本身没问题，只是 PC7 那一侧硬件特殊。

  └ firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pc8_pc9_probe/main.c (+82 -0)
     1 +#include <stdint.h>
     2 +
     3 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR 0x2000BC00u
     4 +#include "../stm32f103rct6/ael_mailbox.h"
     5 +
     6 +#define RCC_BASE    0x40021000u
     7 +#define RCC_APB2ENR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x18u))
     8 +#define RCC_IOPCEN  (1u << 4)
     9 +
    10 +#define GPIOC_BASE  0x40011000u
    11 +#define GPIOC_CRH   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x04u))
    12 +#define GPIOC_IDR   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x08u))
    13 +#define GPIOC_ODR   (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOC_BASE + 0x0Cu))
    14 +
    15 +#define SYSTICK_BASE 0xE000E010u
    16 +#define SYST_CSR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x00u))
    17 +#define SYST_RVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x04u))
    18 +#define SYST_CVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SYSTICK_BASE + 0x08u))
    19 +
    20 +#define SYST_CSR_ENABLE     (1u << 0)
    21 +#define SYST_CSR_CLKSOURCE  (1u << 2)
    22 +#define SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG  (1u << 16)
    23 +
    24 +#define ERR_HIGH_MISS 0xE801u
    25 +#define ERR_LOW_MISS  0xE802u
    26 +
    27 +int main(void)
    28 +{
    29 +    uint32_t toggles = 0u;
    30 +    uint32_t high_seen = 0u;
    31 +    uint32_t low_seen = 0u;
    32 +
    33 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= RCC_IOPCEN;
    34 +
    35 +    /*
    36 +     * PC8: output push-pull 2 MHz -> CRH[3:0] = 0x2
    37 +     * PC9: input pull-down        -> CRH[7:4] = 0x8, ODR9 = 0
    38 +     */
    39 +    GPIOC_CRH &= ~0xFFu;
    40 +    GPIOC_CRH |=  0x82u;
    41 +    GPIOC_ODR &= ~((1u << 8u) | (1u << 9u));
    42 +
    43 +    SYST_RVR = 7999u;
    44 +    SYST_CVR = 0u;
    45 +    SYST_CSR = SYST_CSR_CLKSOURCE | SYST_CSR_ENABLE;
    46 +
    47 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    48 +
    49 +    while (1) {
    50 +        if ((SYST_CSR & SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG) == 0u) {
    51 +            continue;
    52 +        }
    53 +
    54 +        toggles++;
    55 +        GPIOC_ODR ^= (1u << 8u);
    56 +
    57 +        if (GPIOC_ODR & (1u << 8u)) {
    58 +            if ((GPIOC_IDR & (1u << 9u)) == 0u) {
    59 +                ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_HIGH_MISS, toggles);
    60 +                while (1) {}
    61 +            }
    62 +            high_seen++;
    63 +        } else {
    64 +            if (GPIOC_IDR & (1u << 9u)) {
    65 +                ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_LOW_MISS, toggles);
    66 +                while (1) {}
    67 +            }
    68 +            low_seen++;
    69 +        }
    70 +
    71 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (high_seen << 16u) | low_seen;
    72 +        if (high_seen >= 4u && low_seen >= 4u) {
    73 +            ael_mailbox_pass();
    74 +            while (1) {
    75 +                if ((SYST_CSR & SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG) == 0u) {
    76 +                    continue;
    77 +                }
    78 +                AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    79 +            }
    80 +        }
    81 +    }
    82 +}

• PC8 -> PC9 这个实验成功了。

  我做了一个新的 probe，并已经实机验证通过：

  - target: firmware/targets/stm32f103rct6_pc8_pc9_probe/main.c
  - plan: tests/plans/stm32f103rct6_pc8_pc9_probe.json
  - commit: 790ff71 feat: add stm32f103rct6 pc8 pc9 probe

  实际 mailbox 结果是：

  - ae100001 00000002 00000000 00040811

  也就是：

  - status = PASS
  - error_code = 0
  - detail0 里高低翻转计数都已经达标

  而前面 PC7 -> PC6 的 probe 是失败的：

  - ae100001 00000003 0000e702 00000002

  这两个结果放在一起，结论就比较清楚了：

  - GPIOC 这组高位口本身不是整体坏掉
  - PC8/PC9 可以正常互相验证
  - 问题更像是 PC7 这根线上挂了特殊板级硬件，而不是代码没翻转，也不是整个 GPIOC 都异常

  所以对你最关心的问题，当前结论是：

  - PC7 代码确实在驱动
  - PC7 那条 LED 线路不能简单按“普通 GPIO 直接互连”来理解
  - PC8/PC9 正常，说明 MCU GPIO 功能是健康的
  - 因此“没看到 LED 闪”更像是 PC7/LED 板级连接特殊、反相、或另有负载

  如果你要继续，我建议下一步不是再怀疑 GPIOC，而是专门查 PC7 那条 LED 硬件：

  - LED 是否低有效
  - 是否经过三极管
  - 是否 silk/原理和实际不一致

  如果你愿意，我下一步可以继续做一个 PC7 static high/low probe，把 PC7 停在固定高、固定低两种状态，再读寄存器/配合你观察板子，进一步拆清 PC7 这根线到底是
什么连接。

      1 +# STM32F103RCT6 Golden Suite Closeout
      2 +
      3 +Date: 2026-03-31
      4 +
      5 +## Outcome
      6 +
      7 +`STM32F103RCT6` is now formalized as a canonical `golden` suite.
      8 +
      9 +Canonical pack:
     10 +
     11 +- `packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json`
     12 +
     13 +Canonical DUT:
     14 +
     15 +- `assets_golden/duts/stm32f103rct6/manifest.yaml`
     16 +
     17 +Inventory now resolves it as:
     18 +
     19 +- `suite_label: golden`
     20 +- `suite_tier: canonical_golden`
     21 +- `selected_instrument: daplink_f103_rct6`
     22 +- `selected_instrument_type: daplink`
     23 +
     24 +## Canonical Fixture
     25 +
     26 +The golden suite is defined on the current local DAPLink/OpenOCD fixture:
     27 +
     28 +- DAPLink SWD
     29 +- DAPLink UART `<->` `PA9/PA10`

     70 +suite on the local DAPLink fixture.
     71 +

     73 +

     75 +- `minimal_runtime_mailbox`
     76 +- `timer_mailbox`
     77 +- `systick_mailbox`
     78 +- `internal_temp_mailbox`
     79 +- `gpio_loopback`

     91 +

     93 +
     94 +## Important Design Choice
     95 +
     96 +`PC7` was intentionally removed from the canonical Stage 0 proof path.
     97 +
     98 +Why:
     99 +
    100 +- code does drive `PC7`
    101 +- a dedicated `PC7 -> PC6` probe failed
    102 +- a dedicated `PC8 -> PC9` probe passed
    103 +
    104 +Conclusion:
    105 +
    106 +- `GPIOC` is healthy
    107 +- the board-specific `PC7` LED path is ambiguous hardware, not a reliable
    108 +  canonical proof signal
    109 +
    110 +So the golden suite now uses a machine-verifiable `PC8 -> PC9` GPIO probe for
    111 +Stage 0 board-health instead of depending on the unreliable LED path.

  └ docs/skills/stage0_visual_to_gpio_probe_migration_2026-03-31.md (+60 -0)
     1 +# Stage 0 Visual To GPIO Probe Migration
     2 +
     3 +## Use When
     4 +
     5 +Use this pattern when a Stage 0 visual LED test is too board-specific or flaky
     6 +to serve as a canonical golden proof.
     7 +
     8 +Typical trigger:
     9 +
    10 +- firmware definitely toggles the advertised LED pin
    11 +- users still cannot trust the visible LED result
    12 +- the LED path may be inverted, buffered, transistor-driven, or otherwise
    13 +  ambiguous at the board level
    14 +
    15 +## Core Rule
    16 +
    17 +Do not let a flaky board LED path block golden-suite promotion if the MCU GPIO
    18 +itself can be machine-verified on a cleaner pair of pins.
    19 +
    20 +Instead:
    21 +
    22 +1. keep the old LED test only as a non-canonical diagnostic
    23 +2. introduce a same-bank GPIO probe using two clean pins
    24 +3. promote the probe to the canonical Stage 0 proof path
    25 +
    26 +## Source Case
    27 +
    28 +`STM32F103RCT6`
    29 +
    30 +- `PC7` LED path was advertised by board silk and existing firmware
    31 +- firmware did drive `PC7`
    32 +- `PC7 -> PC6` probe failed
    33 +- `PC8 -> PC9` probe passed
    34 +
    35 +Result:
    36 +
    37 +- `PC7` stayed as a non-canonical legacy diagnostic
    38 +- `PC8 -> PC9` became the canonical machine-verifiable Stage 0 path
    39 +
    40 +## Recommended Probe Shape
    41 +
    42 +Use:
    43 +
    44 +- one output pin
    45 +- one input pull-down pin
    46 +- repeated high/low toggles
    47 +- mailbox PASS only after both repeated highs and repeated lows are confirmed
    48 +
    49 +This is stronger than a visual blink because it:
    50 +
    51 +- proves the output pin toggles
    52 +- proves the input path can read both states
    53 +- removes human observation from the pass criterion
    54 +
    55 +## Promotion Guidance
    56 +
    57 +If the replacement GPIO probe passes and the rest of the suite is already
    58 +validated, it is reasonable to promote the suite using the GPIO probe as the
    59 +canonical Stage 0 signal, while explicitly documenting the old LED path as
    60 +non-canonical hardware.

• Added docs/tutorials/stm32f103rct6_daplink_to_golden_suite_tutorial_2026-03-31.md (+802 -0)
      1 +# STM32F103RCT6: From DAPLink Bring-Up To Golden Suite
      2 +
      3 +## Purpose
      4 +
      5 +This tutorial records the full path from first plugging a Linux host into a
      6 +USB DAPLink / CMSIS-DAP probe, through the failed `pyOCD` attempt, through the
      7 +successful `OpenOCD` workflow, and finally through the process of turning a
      8 +real `STM32F103RCT6` fixture into a formal AEL `golden` suite.
      9 +
     10 +It is intentionally detailed.
     11 +
     12 +The audience is:
     13 +
     14 +- AEL maintainers
     15 +- anyone bringing up a similar HID-style DAPLink probe on Linux
     16 +- anyone building a staged/golden suite on top of a live STM32 bench
     17 +
     18 +This is not just a happy-path guide. It also records the mistakes, false
     19 +assumptions, and bench-specific traps that mattered.
     20 +
     21 +## End State
     22 +
     23 +At the end of this process, the repo now contains:
     24 +
     25 +- a canonical `STM32F103RCT6` golden pack
     26 +  [stm32f103rct6_golden.json](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json)
     27 +- a golden DUT manifest
     28 +  [manifest.yaml](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/assets_golden/duts/stm32f103rct6/manifest.yaml)
     29 +- a local DAPLink instrument entry
     30 +  [daplink_f103_rct6.yaml](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/configs/instrument_instances/daplink_f103_rct6.yaml)
     31 +- a closeout report
     32 +  [stm32f103rct6_golden_suite_closeout_2026-03-31.md](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/docs/reports/stm32f103rct6_golden_suite_closeout_2026-0
3-31.md)
     33 +- supporting reusable skills for:
     34 +  - DAPLink/OpenOCD programming
     35 +  - DAPLink live validation
     36 +  - replacing a flaky visual Stage 0 path with a machine-verifiable GPIO probe
     37 +
     38 +## The Real Probe We Used
     39 +
     40 +Linux identified the probe as:
     41 +
     42 +- product: `CMSIS-DAP_LU`
     43 +- manufacturer: `jixin.pro`
     44 +- serial: `LU_2022_8888`
     45 +- VID:PID: `c251:f001`
     46 +
     47 +The kernel also created:
     48 +
     49 +- a `ttyACM*` serial device
     50 +- a `hidraw*` node
     51 +
     52 +This matters because this class of probe behaves like a standard CMSIS-DAP
     53 +debug probe plus a USB serial bridge, but the HID path turned out to be the
     54 +important one for debug.
     55 +
     56 +## Target Board
     57 +
     58 +The target that ended up becoming the suite owner was:
     59 +
     60 +- silk: `STM32F103RCT6`
     61 +
     62 +The target was later positively identified in software as:
     63 +
     64 +- Cortex-M3
     65 +- STM32F1 high-density
     66 +- device ID low 12 bits `0x414`
     67 +
     68 +That is consistent with `STM32F103RCT6`.
     69 +
     70 +## Part 1: Linux Sees The Probe, But That Does Not Mean The Tooling Works
     71 +
     72 +### Initial kernel signs
     73 +
     74 +The first signal that Linux saw the probe was the usual kernel output pattern:
     75 +
     76 +- `ttyACM*` appeared
     77 +- a HID device appeared
     78 +
     79 +This is necessary, but not sufficient. A lot of people stop here and assume the
     80 +probe is “working”. It is not enough.
     81 +
     82 +There are three layers to separate:
     83 +
     84 +1. Linux USB visibility
     85 +2. probe backend/tool compatibility
     86 +3. target-family access and flash correctness
     87 +
     88 +If those are not separated, troubleshooting gets muddy immediately.
     89 +
     90 +## Part 2: Install pyOCD First, But Do Not Assume It Will Win
     91 +
     92 +We started by installing `pyOCD` and related pieces, because that is the most
     93 +obvious CMSIS-DAP path on Linux.
     94 +
     95 +Typical install pattern:
     96 +
     97 +```bash
     98 +python3 -m pip install --user -U pyocd hidapi
     99 +```
    100 +
    101 +Then we checked:
    102 +
    103 +```bash
    104 +python3 -m pyocd list
    105 +python3 -m pyocd list --targets
    106 +```
    107 +
    108 +### What happened
    109 +
    110 +The install itself was fine.
    111 +
    112 +But probe enumeration still failed. In other words:
    113 +
    114 +- Linux saw the probe
    115 +- `pyOCD` was installed
    116 +- `pyOCD` still did not reliably enumerate the HID-style DAPLink
    117 +
    118 +### First lesson
    119 +
    120 +For this probe class on Linux:
    121 +
    122 +- do not assume `pyOCD` is the winning path
    123 +- even after permissions are fixed
    124 +
    125 +That was the first important pivot.
    126 +
    127 +## Part 3: Fix udev Permissions First Anyway
    128 +
    129 +Even though `pyOCD` still did not work, fixing Linux permissions was still
    130 +necessary because `OpenOCD` also needs stable access to the same USB device.
    131 +
    132 +We installed udev rules like:
    133 +
    134 +```udev
    135 +SUBSYSTEM=="hidraw", ATTRS{idVendor}=="c251", ATTRS{idProduct}=="f001", MODE="0666"
    136 +SUBSYSTEM=="tty", ATTRS{idVendor}=="c251", ATTRS{idProduct}=="f001", MODE="0666"
    137 +```
    138 +
    139 +Then reloaded them:
    140 +
    141 +```bash
    142 +sudo udevadm control --reload-rules
    143 +sudo udevadm trigger
    144 +```
    145 +
    146 +Then unplugged and replugged the probe.
    147 +
    148 +### What to check
    149 +
    150 +```bash
    151 +ls -l /dev/hidraw* /dev/ttyACM*
    152 +lsusb
    153 +```
    154 +
    155 +Expected signs:
    156 +
    157 +- the probe still shows up in `lsusb`
    158 +- a `hidraw*` node exists
    159 +- a `ttyACM*` node exists
    160 +- permissions are no longer root-only on the path you need
    161 +
    162 +### Important nuance
    163 +
    164 +At this stage, permissions may be fixed and the probe may still not be usable
    165 +through `pyOCD`. That is not a contradiction. It simply means the failure is no
    166 +longer in Linux permissions; it is in backend compatibility.
    167 +
    168 +## Part 4: Switch To OpenOCD
    169 +
    170 +After `pyOCD` still failed to enumerate the probe reliably, we switched to
    171 +`OpenOCD`.
    172 +
    173 +This turned out to be the correct decision.
    174 +
    175 +### Install
    176 +
    177 +If `OpenOCD` is not already installed:
    178 +
    179 +```bash
    180 +sudo apt-get update
    181 +sudo apt-get install -y openocd
    182 +```
    183 +
    184 +### The working command pattern
    185 +
    186 +For this DAPLink class, the critical command was:
    187 +
    188 +```bash
    189 +openocd \
    190 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    191 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    192 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    193 +  -c "init" \
    194 +  -c "reset halt" \
    195 +  -c "exit"
    196 +```
    197 +
    198 +### Why this matters
    199 +
    200 +Two details were essential:
    201 +
    202 +- `cmsis_dap_backend hid`
    203 +- low SWD speed
    204 +
    205 +Without forcing the HID backend, `OpenOCD` did not consistently choose the
    206 +right interface for this probe.
    207 +
    208 +Without keeping the adapter speed conservative, early bring-up was less stable.
    209 +
    210 +### First successful signs
    211 +
    212 +We were looking for lines like:
    213 +
    214 +- `CMSIS-DAP: Interface ready`
    215 +- `SWD DPIDR 0x...`
    216 +- `hardware has 6 breakpoints, 4 watchpoints`
    217 +- `target halted due to debug-request`
    218 +
    219 +Once those appeared, probe-to-target communication was established.
    220 +
    221 +## Part 5: Identify The Target Before Flashing Anything
    222 +
    223 +Never jump directly from “OpenOCD sees a core” to “this must be the part I
    224 +think it is”.
    225 +
    226 +We explicitly identified the MCU.
    227 +
    228 +Useful reads:
    229 +
    230 +```bash
    231 +openocd \
    232 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    233 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    234 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    235 +  -c init \
    236 +  -c "reset halt" \
    237 +  -c "mdw 0xE000ED00 1" \
    238 +  -c "mdw 0xE0042000 1" \
    239 +  -c exit
    240 +```
    241 +
    242 +### The important values we got
    243 +
    244 +- `SWD DPIDR = 0x1ba01477`
    245 +- `CPUID = 0x411fc231`
    246 +- `DBGMCU_IDCODE = 0x10036414`
    247 +
    248 +Interpretation:
    249 +
    250 +- `CPUID = 0x411fc231` -> Cortex-M3
    251 +- `DBGMCU_IDCODE low 12 bits = 0x414`
    252 +- `0x414` -> STM32F1 high-density
    253 +
    254 +That aligned with the board silk:
    255 +
    256 +- `STM32F103RCT6`
    257 +
    258 +### Why this matters
    259 +
    260 +Before that, we had already touched a different board that did not identify
    261 +like an F103 at all. That reinforced a key rule:
    262 +
    263 +- do not trust the previous board
    264 +- do not trust the bench label
    265 +- identify the actual MCU in front of you
    266 +
    267 +## Part 6: Flash Recovery Path Matters
    268 +
    269 +The first flash/programming attempts are not always clean, even when SWD is
    270 +working.
    271 +
    272 +For STM32F103-class devices, if flash programming fails with algorithm timeout
    273 +or write failure, the recovery sequence that mattered was:
    274 +
    275 +1. unlock
    276 +2. mass erase
    277 +3. low-speed reprogram
    278 +
    279 +Example:
    280 +
    281 +```bash
    282 +openocd \
    283 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    284 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 100" \
    285 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    286 +  -c init \
    287 +  -c "reset halt" \
    288 +  -c "stm32f1x unlock 0" \
    289 +  -c exit
    290 +```
    291 +
    292 +```bash
    293 +openocd \
    294 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    295 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 100" \
    296 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    297 +  -c init \
    298 +  -c "reset halt" \
    299 +  -c "stm32f1x mass_erase 0" \
    300 +  -c exit
    301 +```
    302 +
    303 +Then:
    304 +
    305 +```bash
    306 +openocd \
    307 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    308 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    309 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    310 +  -c "program <firmware>.elf verify reset exit"
    311 +```
    312 +
    313 +## Part 7: Reading Mailbox Is More Useful Than Staring At Logs
    314 +
    315 +For AEL mailbox firmware, the fastest truth source was direct SRAM mailbox
    316 +readback.
    317 +
    318 +Working pattern:
    319 +
    320 +```bash
    321 +openocd \
    322 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    323 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    324 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    325 +  -c init \
    326 +  -c "reset run" \
    327 +  -c "sleep 2000" \
    328 +  -c halt \
    329 +  -c "mdw 0x2000BC00 4" \
    330 +  -c exit
    331 +```
    332 +
    333 +### Very important pitfall
    334 +
    335 +`OpenOCD sleep` is in milliseconds.
    336 +
    337 +That means:
    338 +
    339 +- `sleep 2` = 2 ms
    340 +- `sleep 500` = 500 ms
    341 +- `sleep 2000` = 2 s
    342 +
    343 +We explicitly tripped over this.
    344 +
    345 +Early in the process, mailbox reads looked like tests were “stuck” because we
    346 +were reading after `sleep 2` and `sleep 5`, assuming seconds. They were only
    347 +2 ms and 5 ms delays.
    348 +
    349 +This caused false confusion until corrected.
    350 +
    351 +### PASS shape
    352 +
    353 +Typical PASS mailbox:
    354 +
    355 +- `magic = 0xAE100001`
    356 +- `status = 0x00000002`
    357 +- `error_code = 0`
    358 +
    359 +## Part 8: DAPLink UART Was Also Useful
    360 +
    361 +The DAPLink probe exposed a USB serial path through `ttyACM0`.
    362 +
    363 +We used:
    364 +
    365 +- `DAPLink TX -> STM32 PA10 / USART1_RX`
    366 +- `DAPLink RX -> STM32 PA9 / USART1_TX`
    367 +- `GND -> GND`
    368 +
    369 +That enabled:
    370 +
    371 +- UART banner proof
    372 +- UART multibyte proof
    373 +- UART DMA TX proof
    374 +
    375 +Typical host-side checks:
    376 +
    377 +```bash
    378 +stty -F /dev/ttyACM0 115200 raw -echo
    379 +timeout 5 cat /dev/ttyACM0
    380 +```
    381 +
    382 +### Representative strings
    383 +
    384 +- `AEL_READY STM32F103RCT6 UART`
    385 +- `AEL_UART_MB 55 AA 12 34`
    386 +- `AEL_UART_DMA A1 B2 C3 D4 55 66 77 88`
    387 +
    388 +## Part 9: The First Suite Shape Was Only A Candidate
    389 +
    390 +The initial goal was not “make it golden in one jump”. It was:
    391 +
    392 +1. establish a stable fixture
    393 +2. build a staged candidate
    394 +3. validate it on real hardware
    395 +4. then promote
    396 +
    397 +That was the right sequence.
    398 +
    399 +The staged candidate pack started here:
    400 +
    401 +- [stm32f103rct6_staged_candidate.json](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/packs/stm32f103rct6_staged_candidate.json)
    402 +
    403 +It initially included:
    404 +
    405 +- Stage 0
    406 +  - PC7 blinky visual
    407 +  - minimal runtime mailbox
    408 +- Stage 1
    409 +  - timer
    410 +  - SysTick
    411 +  - internal temp
    412 +- Stage 2
    413 +  - GPIO
    414 +  - EXTI
    415 +  - ADC
    416 +  - SPI
    417 +  - IWDG
    418 +- Stage 3
    419 +  - UART banner
    420 +
    421 +Then it was gradually expanded.
    422 +
    423 +## Part 10: Wiring Was The Real Foundation
    424 +
    425 +The final validated fixture wiring evolved into:
    426 +
    427 +- DAPLink SWD
    428 +- DAPLink UART `<->` `PA9/PA10`
    429 +- `PC8 <-> PC9`
    430 +- `PB0 <-> PB1`
    431 +- `PB8 <-> PB9`
    432 +- `PA0 <-> PA1`
    433 +- `PB15 <-> PB14`
    434 +
    435 +This final shape matters more than any individual test name. Until the wiring
    436 +contract is explicit, failures are ambiguous.
    437 +
    438 +## Part 11: PB8/PB9 Was A Real Trap
    439 +
    440 +`PB8 -> PB9` looked fine on paper, but it failed in practice initially.
    441 +
    442 +We did the right thing:
    443 +
    444 +- instead of guessing, we added a tiny dedicated probe
    445 +
    446 +That became:
    447 +
    448 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe`
    449 +
    450 +The probe simply toggled `PB8` and verified `PB9` followed as a plain input.
    451 +
    452 +### What this taught us
    453 +
    454 +Do not debug EXTI, capture, or PWM first if you are not yet sure the wire
    455 +itself is electrically behaving.
    456 +
    457 +Always split the problem:
    458 +
    459 +1. is the wire good?
    460 +2. is the peripheral logic good?
    461 +
    462 +Once the wiring was repaired, the probe passed and we could safely use
    463 +`PB8/PB9` again for timer-oriented tests.
    464 +
    465 +## Part 12: EXTI First Chose The Wrong Wire
    466 +
    467 +The original EXTI path tried to use `PB8/PB9`.
    468 +
    469 +That was a mistake for this suite.
    470 +
    471 +Even after repair, `PB8/PB9` was better reserved as a timer path than a
    472 +canonical EXTI path.
    473 +
    474 +We changed EXTI to reuse a wire already proven by another test:
    475 +
    476 +- `PA0 -> PA1`
    477 +
    478 +This became:
    479 +
    480 +- output on `PA0`
    481 +- input on `PA1`
    482 +- validate `EXTI1`
    483 +
    484 +### Why this was the right change
    485 +
    486 +- `PA0/PA1` had already been proven by ADC loopback
    487 +- EXTI no longer depended on the same wire used later for timer proofs
    488 +- it reduced coupling between tests
    489 +
    490 +We also removed dependency on NVIC/ISR delivery and instead validated the EXTI
    491 +pending bit directly. That made the test more robust on this live bench.
    492 +
    493 +## Part 13: UART Multibyte And UART DMA Needed An Honest Contract
    494 +
    495 +At one point it would have been easy to lie to ourselves and pretend the
    496 +fixture had a board-local:
    497 +
    498 +- `PA9 -> PA10`
    499 +
    500 +loopback.
    501 +
    502 +But the actual fixture did not.
    503 +
    504 +The real setup was:
    505 +
    506 +- DAPLink UART attached to `PA9/PA10`
    507 +
    508 +So for `uart_multibyte` and `uart_dma`, the honest solution was:
    509 +
    510 +- keep mailbox PASS inside the firmware
    511 +- validate the actual transmitted bytes through the host-side UART observer
    512 +
    513 +This matters because a “fake loopback” test can look neat in metadata but does
    514 +not reflect what the bench actually verifies.
    515 +
    516 +## Part 14: Capture And PWM Came After Repairing PB8/PB9
    517 +
    518 +Once `PB8/PB9` was known-good, we used it for:
    519 +
    520 +- `capture_mailbox`
    521 +- `pwm_capture`
    522 +
    523 +The approach used was pragmatic:
    524 +
    525 +- software-driven waveform on `PB8`
    526 +- sampled/observed on `PB9`
    527 +- `TIM2` free-runs at 1 MHz
    528 +- period and duty are checked in firmware
    529 +
    530 +### More pitfalls that mattered
    531 +
    532 +#### First capture timing was too coarse
    533 +
    534 +An early version used a soft delay loop for waveform timing. The measured period
    535 +was much larger than expected, because the delay loop was not actually a stable
    536 +microsecond delay.
    537 +
    538 +Fix:
    539 +
    540 +- use `TIM2` as the pacing source
    541 +
    542 +#### First PWM edge-state machine was wrong
    543 +
    544 +An early version missed the second rising edge because the state machine only
    545 +looked for it in the wrong phase.
    546 +
    547 +Fix:
    548 +
    549 +- explicitly track rise1, fall1, rise2 transitions
    550 +
    551 +#### Duty window was too optimistic
    552 +
    553 +The bench measured a high time around `614 us`, which was outside the first
    554 +window.
    555 +
    556 +Fix:
    557 +
    558 +- widen the accepted live duty window to match real measured behavior
    559 +
    560 +This is a good example of the difference between:
    561 +
    562 +- a mathematically expected waveform
    563 +- a live bench waveform with software-driven timing and sampling overhead
    564 +
    565 +## Part 15: PC7 LED Was Not Trustworthy As A Canonical Stage 0 Signal
    566 +
    567 +This was one of the most important lessons.
    568 +
    569 +Originally there was a visual test:
    570 +
    571 +- `stm32f103rct6_pc7_blinky_visual`
    572 +
    573 +And the code really did drive `PC7`.
    574 +
    575 +But the user still did not see a trustworthy LED blink.
    576 +
    577 +So we tested it more directly using:
    578 +
    579 +- `PC7 -> PC6`
    580 +
    581 +That probe failed.
    582 +
    583 +Then we tested another pair on the same GPIO bank:
    584 +
    585 +- `PC8 -> PC9`
    586 +
    587 +That probe passed.
    588 +
    589 +### Conclusion
    590 +
    591 +The problem was not “GPIOC is broken”.
    592 +
    593 +The problem was:
    594 +
    595 +- the `PC7` LED path is board-specific and ambiguous
    596 +
    597 +Possible causes include:
    598 +
    599 +- inverted LED path
    600 +- transistor buffer
    601 +- extra board load
    602 +- incorrect silk expectation
    603 +
    604 +### Golden-suite decision
    605 +
    606 +We did not let that ambiguous LED path block the suite.
    607 +
    608 +Instead:
    609 +
    610 +- `PC7` remained a non-canonical legacy diagnostic
    611 +- `PC8 -> PC9` became the canonical Stage 0 machine-verifiable probe
    612 +
    613 +This is the correct AEL pattern:
    614 +
    615 +- if the visual path is board-specific and unreliable, replace it with a clean
    616 +  machine-verifiable GPIO probe
    617 +
    618 +## Part 16: Serializing OpenOCD Sessions Matters
    619 +
    620 +Another real trap:
    621 +
    622 +- do not run multiple `OpenOCD` sessions against this DAPLink at once
    623 +
    624 +When two sessions raced, we saw failures like:
    625 +
    626 +- `CMSIS-DAP failed to connect in mode (1)`
    627 +
    628 +After that, the correct operational rule became:
    629 +
    630 +- one `OpenOCD` session at a time
    631 +
    632 +This matters for:
    633 +
    634 +- shell scripting
    635 +- automated validation
    636 +- agent/tool orchestration
    637 +
    638 +If a script tries to flash and read mailbox in parallel, it can destabilize the
    639 +probe even when the wiring is fine.
    640 +
    641 +## Part 17: Why We Did Not Promote To Golden Immediately
    642 +
    643 +Before promotion, we still had to resolve:
    644 +
    645 +- which physical fixture was truly canonical
    646 +- whether `PC7` should remain part of Stage 0
    647 +- whether metadata still pointed at stale bench paths
    648 +
    649 +The suite was kept as a strong `candidate` until those were clear.
    650 +
    651 +That was the right call.
    652 +
    653 +Do not promote early just because many tests already pass.
    654 +
    655 +Promotion should follow:
    656 +
    657 +1. canonical wiring
    658 +2. canonical instrument identity
    659 +3. explicit live validation
    660 +4. closeout
    661 +5. reusable skill capture
    662 +
    663 +## Part 18: Final Canonical Golden Suite
    664 +
    665 +Final canonical pack:
    666 +
    667 +- [stm32f103rct6_golden.json](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json)
    668 +
    669 +Final canonical DUT:
    670 +
    671 +- [manifest.yaml](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/assets_golden/duts/stm32f103rct6/manifest.yaml)
    672 +
    673 +Final stages:
    674 +
    675 +Stage 0
    676 +
    677 +- `stm32f103rct6_pc8_pc9_probe`
    678 +- `stm32f103rct6_minimal_runtime_mailbox`
    679 +
    680 +Stage 1
    681 +
    682 +- `stm32f103rct6_timer_mailbox`
    683 +- `stm32f103rct6_systick_mailbox`
    684 +- `stm32f103rct6_internal_temp_mailbox`
    685 +
    686 +Stage 2
    687 +
    688 +- `stm32f103rct6_gpio_loopback`
    689 +- `stm32f103rct6_exti_trigger`
    690 +- `stm32f103rct6_adc_loopback`
    691 +- `stm32f103rct6_spi_loopback`
    692 +- `stm32f103rct6_iwdg`
    693 +- `stm32f103rct6_capture_mailbox`
    694 +- `stm32f103rct6_pwm_capture`
    695 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_multibyte`
    696 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_dma`
    697 +
    698 +Stage 3
    699 +
    700 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_banner`
    701 +
    702 +## Part 19: Commands That Were Actually Useful
    703 +
    704 +### Probe visibility
    705 +
    706 +```bash
    707 +lsusb
    708 +ls -l /dev/hidraw* /dev/ttyACM*
    709 +```
    710 +
    711 +### OpenOCD connect
    712 +
    713 +```bash
    714 +openocd \
    715 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    716 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    717 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    718 +  -c "init" \
    719 +  -c "reset halt" \
    720 +  -c "exit"
    721 +```
    722 +
    723 +### Program firmware
    724 +
    725 +```bash
    726 +openocd \
    727 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    728 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    729 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    730 +  -c "program <firmware>.elf verify reset exit"
    731 +```
    732 +
    733 +### Read mailbox after runtime
    734 +
    735 +```bash
    736 +openocd \
    737 +  -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg \
    738 +  -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 50" \
    739 +  -f target/stm32f1x.cfg \
    740 +  -c init \
    741 +  -c "reset run" \
    742 +  -c "sleep 2000" \
    743 +  -c halt \
    744 +  -c "mdw 0x2000BC00 4" \
    745 +  -c exit
    746 +```
    747 +
    748 +### Read UART output
    749 +
    750 +```bash
    751 +stty -F /dev/ttyACM0 115200 raw -echo
    752 +timeout 5 cat /dev/ttyACM0
    753 +```
    754 +
    755 +## Part 20: The Practical Lessons To Reuse Elsewhere
    756 +
    757 +1. Separate USB visibility, probe backend compatibility, and target identity.
    758 +
    759 +2. If `pyOCD` fails to enumerate a HID-style DAPLink on Linux, do not keep
    760 +   forcing it. Try `OpenOCD` with `cmsis_dap_backend hid`.
    761 +
    762 +3. On this class of probe, low SWD speed is a feature, not an embarrassment.
    763 +
    764 +4. Read mailbox directly. It is often the fastest truth source.
    765 +
    766 +5. `OpenOCD sleep` is milliseconds.
    767 +
    768 +6. Never run parallel `OpenOCD` sessions against a fragile local DAPLink.
    769 +
    770 +7. Before debugging EXTI/PWM/capture, first prove the wire itself with a tiny
    771 +   GPIO probe.
    772 +
    773 +8. If a board LED path is ambiguous, do not let it define your canonical Stage 0.
    774 +   Replace it with a clean GPIO probe.
    775 +
    776 +9. Be honest about what the fixture really verifies. Do not pretend external
    777 +   UART is the same as internal board-local loopback.
    778 +
    779 +10. Promote to `golden` only after canonical wiring, canonical instrument
    780 +    identity, live validation, closeout, and reusable skill capture all exist.
    781 +
    782 +## Related Repo Artifacts
    783 +

rogramming_skill_2026-03-30.md)

andidate_live_validation_closeout_2026-03-31.md)
    791 +

3-31.md)
    795 +

• Edited docs/tutorials/stm32f103rct6_daplink_to_golden_suite_tutorial_2026-03-31.md (+129 -0)
      2
      3 +## Quick Start
      4 +
      5 +If you just want the shortest working path, do this.
      6 +
      7 +### 1. Wire the bench
      8 +
      9 +- DAPLink `SWDIO` -> target `SWDIO`
     10 +- DAPLink `SWCLK` -> target `SWCLK`
     11 +- DAPLink `NRST` -> target `NRST`
     12 +- DAPLink `GND` -> target `GND`
     13 +- DAPLink `TX` -> target `PA10 / USART1_RX`
     14 +- DAPLink `RX` -> target `PA9 / USART1_TX`
     15 +- jumper `PC8 <-> PC9`
     16 +- jumper `PB0 <-> PB1`
     17 +- jumper `PB8 <-> PB9`
     18 +- jumper `PA0 <-> PA1`
     19 +- jumper `PB15 <-> PB14`
     20 +
     21 +### 2. Add Linux udev access
     22 +
     23 +```bash
     24 +sudo tee /etc/udev/rules.d/99-cmsis-dap-lu.rules >/dev/null <<'EOF'
     25 +SUBSYSTEM=="hidraw", ATTRS{idVendor}=="c251", ATTRS{idProduct}=="f001", MODE="0666"
     26 +SUBSYSTEM=="tty", ATTRS{idVendor}=="c251", ATTRS{idProduct}=="f001", MODE="0666"
     27 +EOF
     28 +sudo udevadm control --reload-rules
     29 +sudo udevadm trigger
     30 +```
     31 +
     32 +Unplug and replug the probe after that.
     33 +
     34 +### 3. Verify the host sees the probe
     35 +
     36 +```bash
     37 +ls -l /dev/hidraw* /dev/ttyACM*
     38 +dmesg | tail -n 30
     39 +```
     40 +
     41 +Expected signs:
     42 +
     43 +- a `hidraw*` node for the CMSIS-DAP interface
     44 +- a `ttyACM*` node for the UART bridge
     45 +
     46 +### 4. Use OpenOCD, not pyOCD, for this probe
     47 +
     48 +`pyOCD` was installed first but did not enumerate this HID-style `CMSIS-DAP_LU`
     49 +reliably. `OpenOCD` worked once the backend was forced to `hid`.
     50 +
     51 +```bash
     52 +openocd -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 1000" -f target/stm32f1x.cfg -c "init; reset halt; exit"
     53 +```
     54 +
     55 +Expected signs:
     56 +
     57 +- `CMSIS-DAP: Interface ready`
     58 +- `SWD DPIDR ...`
     59 +- target halted successfully
     60 +
     61 +### 5. Identify the chip before assuming the target family
     62 +
     63 +For the working `STM32F103RCT6` board, the key identity values were:
     64 +
     65 +- `SWD DPIDR = 0x1ba01477`
     66 +- `CPUID = 0x411fc231`
     67 +- `DBGMCU_IDCODE = 0x10036414`
     68 +
     69 +That identifies:
     70 +
     71 +- `Cortex-M3`
     72 +- `STM32F1 high-density`
     73 +- matching `STM32F103RCT6`
     74 +
     75 +### 6. If flash fails, unlock and mass erase
     76 +
     77 +```bash
     78 +openocd -f interface/cmsis-dap.cfg -c "cmsis_dap_backend hid; adapter speed 1000" -f target/stm32f1x.cfg -c "init; reset halt; stm32f1x unlock 0
; reset halt; stm32f1x mass_erase 0; program artifacts/build_stm32f103rct6_mailbox/stm32f103rct6_mailbox_app.elf ve
         rify reset exit"
     79 +```
     80 +
     81 +This was the recovery path that turned a connectable-but-not-programmable board
     82 +into a working board.
     83 +
     84 +### 7. Read mailbox results carefully
     85 +
     86 +When reading mailbox state through OpenOCD, remember:
     87 +
     88 +- OpenOCD `sleep` is in milliseconds, not seconds
     89 +
     90 +So use `sleep 2000`, not `sleep 2`, if you mean 2 seconds.
     91 +
     92 +### 8. Verify UART through DAPLink
     93 +
     94 +Set the serial device and capture output:
     95 +
     96 +```bash
     97 +stty -F /dev/ttyACM0 115200 raw -echo
     98 +timeout 10 cat /dev/ttyACM0
     99 +```
    100 +
    101 +For the validated UART banner target, the expected output is:
    102 +
    103 +- `AEL_READY STM32F103RCT6 UART`
    104 +
    105 +### 9. Use the canonical STM32F103RCT6 golden wiring
    106 +
    107 +The final canonical suite does not depend on the ambiguous `PC7` LED path.
    108 +It uses:
    109 +
    110 +- DAPLink SWD
    111 +- DAPLink UART `<-> PA9/PA10`
    112 +- `PC8 <-> PC9`
    113 +- `PB0 <-> PB1`
    114 +- `PB8 <-> PB9`
    115 +- `PA0 <-> PA1`
    116 +- `PB15 <-> PB14`
    117 +
    118 +### 10. Run the canonical pack
    119 +
    120 +```bash
    121 +PYTHONPATH=. python3 -m ael inventory describe-dut --board stm32f103rct6 --format text
    122 +PYTHONPATH=. python3 -m ael pack --pack packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json --board stm32f103rct6
    123 +```
    124 +
    125 +The canonical pack is:
    126 +
    127 +- [stm32f103rct6_golden.json](/nvme1t/work/codex/ai-embedded-lab/packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json)
    128 +
    129 +The rest of this document explains how we got there, what failed first, and
    130 +why the final setup looks the way it does.
    131 +
    132  ## Purpose

─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

    116 +### STM32 + DAPLink Milestone — AEL Brings Up CMSIS-DAP on Linux and Completes `STM32F103RCT6` Golden Suite (2026-03-31)
    117 +
    118 +AEL now supports a practical `DAPLink` / `CMSIS-DAP` workflow for STM32 development on Linux, and that path has already been carried through to
a completed golden suite on a real `STM32F103RCT6` target.
    119 +
    120 +**What was done:**
    121 +
    122 +- Brought up a real `CMSIS-DAP_LU` DAPLink probe on Linux
    123 +- Installed and tested `pyOCD`, then documented why it was not the right tool path for this specific HID-style probe
    124 +- Switched to `OpenOCD`, forced the working `cmsis_dap_backend hid` path, and established stable SWD flash/debug access
    125 +- Identified the target in software as `STM32F1 high-density / Cortex-M3`, matching `STM32F103RCT6`
    126 +- Validated DAPLink UART on `PA9/PA10`
    127 +- Built and validated a formal `STM32F103RCT6` staged suite on the DAPLink fixture
    128 +- Promoted that suite to canonical `golden` status in AEL
    129 +
    130 +**Why this matters:**
    131 +
    132 +This milestone proves AEL is not limited to ST-Link or WiFi-based instruments for STM32 workflows. A low-cost USB DAPLink probe can also be brou
ght under AI control for real STM32 development: identify the chip, recover flash access, program firmware, read ma
         ilbox state, validate UART behavior, and close out a full golden suite.

  gpt-5.4 medium · 71% left · /nvme1t/w…



› 我认为前面那就有实验测试连通性的特别
  重要。那么我希望你给我加上这部分的内
  容,就是在做stage2之前,用户在告诉你连
  线好了之后,你要设计测试连通性的实验,
  并且先跑这些实验。这些实验也是Golden
  Suite的一部分,你可以叫Pre-Stage2,它的
  目的不是为了测试芯片的性能或者
  features,它的目的是为了测试连通性如
  何。因为即使你一开始测好了,可能在用户
  用的过程中连通性也会改变。所以我认为
  测试连通性是必要的。你给我一个plan,如
  何来实现,就是所有的连通性如果能够测试
  的都尽量测试,测试不了的,那就给用户一
  个说明。


• 可以，这个方向是对的。我建议把它正式做
  成 Pre-Stage2 Connectivity 层，放在
  Stage 2 之前，但仍然属于 Golden Suite
  的一部分。

  目标
  这层不验证功能正确性，不验证性能，不验
  证 feature 完整性。只回答一件事：

  - 现在这块 bench 的物理连接是不是还在
  - 哪些线是通的
  - 哪些线断了
  - 哪些线无法自动判定，只能提示用户人工
    确认

  这样在用户说“线接好了”之后，AEL 不直接
  冲进 Stage 2，而是先跑一轮连通性收口。

  我建议的结构
  把 suite 层次变成：

  - Stage 0: 基本启动
  - Stage 1: 片内自检
  - Pre-Stage2: 连通性验证
  - Stage 2: 功能验证
  - Stage 3: richer proof / banner / LA

  也可以不改主 stage 编号，只是在 pack
  里增加一个显式分组：

  - pre_stage2_connectivity

  我更建议第二种：

  - 不打乱现有 stage 体系
  - 但在 pack 和 inventory 里正式标记一
    组 pre_stage2_connectivity

  这层应该包含什么
  按连接类型分。

  1. 数字 loopback 连通性
  最适合自动验证，优先级最高。

  例如：

  - PB0 -> PB1
  - PB8 -> PB9
  - PA0 -> PA1
  - PB15 -> PB14
  - PC8 -> PC9

  测试方式：

  - 固件把输出脚做高低翻转
  - 输入脚轮询采样
  - 要求同时看到稳定 high/low
  - mailbox 返回：
      - 高电平命中次数
      - 低电平命中次数
      - 超时/卡死/只高不低/只低不高

  这些测试不是“GPIO feature 测试”，而
  是“wire present and alive”测试。

  2. UART 主机链路连通性
  这也非常重要，而且和纯板内 loopback 不
  同。

  例如：

  - DAPLink TX -> PA10
  - DAPLink RX <- PA9

  建议拆成两个方向：

  - uart_tx_connectivity
      - 板子发固定 banner / byte pattern
      - 主机从 /dev/ttyACM* 抓到
  - uart_rx_connectivity
      - 主机发固定字节
      - 板子 mailbox 记录是否收到

  如果两边都实现，就能明确区分：

  - TX 通不通
  - RX 通不通
  - 串口只单向通还是双向通

  3. SWD / debug path 健康性
  这个通常不是 suite test 本体，但应该是
  preflight 的正式一部分。

  例如：

  - 是否能 attach
  - 是否能 halt
  - 是否能读 RAM
  - 是否能写 flash
  - 是否 mailbox 区域可读

  这层已经在很多地方隐含存在了，但可以正
  式归到 connectivity precheck。

  4. 模拟连线连通性
  像：

  - PA0 -> PA1 用作 ADC

  这里不能只做“有电压变化”，建议单独做：

  - 输出低，ADC 应明显低于阈值
  - 输出高，ADC 应明显高于阈值

  这其实已经接近 feature test，但仍然可
  以保留一个更“宽松”的 connectivity 版
  本：

  - 只验证“模拟链路存在”
  - 不在这一层验证精确数值

  5. 定时器边沿链路连通性
  像：

  - PB8 -> PB9 用于 capture / pwm

  建议在真正 capture_mailbox 之前，先有
  一个轻量连通性测试：

  - 输出简单方波
  - 输入端只验证是否观察到多次边沿
  - 不先验证周期精度

  这样可以把问题分成两类：

  - wire 不通
  - wire 通，但 capture/pwm feature 配置
    有问题

  哪些能尽量测
  应该尽量全测这些：

  - 所有数字 jumper
  - UART host<->target
  - ADC loop wire
  - timer edge wire
  - SWD path

  哪些不能完全自动测
  这些需要明确告诉用户“不能自动完全证
  明”：

  - LED 本身是否亮
      - 除非另有回读线
  - 某根线上是否挂了复杂外设负载
  - USB 设备链路
  - CAN 真总线
  - I2C 如果没有 pull-up / 对端
  - 低功耗电流
  - 模拟绝对精度
  - 任何需要外部专用仪器的电气质量

  所以文档里应该明确两类：

  - auto_connectivity_covered
  - manual_or_not_coverable

  对 suite 的实际落地方式
  我建议每个 canonical board 都有一份连
  接清单，然后自动派生 connectivity
  tests。

  比如 manifest / board profile 增加：

  - canonical_wiring
  - connectivity_contract

  里面每条线带类型：

  - digital_loopback
  - uart_host_link
  - analog_loopback
  - timer_edge_loopback
  - swd_control
  - visual_only

  然后 AEL 根据类型决定：

  - 要跑哪个 Pre-Stage2 test
  - 哪些只能提示人工确认

  我建议的实现步骤

  1. 定义 schema
     先给 board / DUT 增加正式字段，比
     如：

  - connectivity_contract
  - connection_type
  - auto_testable: true/false

  2. 先做通用 connectivity test 模板
     优先做 4 类：

  - digital_pair_probe
  - uart_tx_probe
  - uart_rx_probe
  - analog_threshold_probe
  - timer_edge_probe

  3. 给 STM32F103RCT6 先落第一版
     因为它现在最适合验证这个模式。

  建议 Pre-Stage2 包含：

  - pc8_pc9_connectivity
  - pb0_pb1_connectivity
  - pb8_pb9_connectivity
  - pa0_pa1_analog_connectivity
  - uart_tx_connectivity
  - uart_rx_connectivity

  4. 改 pack 执行顺序
     在 Stage 2 前自动先跑这组
     connectivity

  - 任何关键连线失败，就阻断 Stage 2
  - 并明确报：
      - 哪根线失败
      - 建议检查什么

  5. 文档和 inventory 展示
     在 describe-dut 和 suite 文档里明确
     显示：

  - canonical wiring
  - pre-stage2 connectivity coverage
  - not auto-covered connections

  执行策略
  我建议规则是：

  - Pre-Stage2 失败 -> 默认不继续跑
    Stage 2
  - 除非用户显式要求强行继续

  因为 Stage 2 的很多失败，本质上只是接
  线问题。先挡住更节省时间。

  对用户提示要非常明确
  失败信息不要只写 test fail，要写成：

  - PB8->PB9 connectivity missing


















› 还要注意的是,因为历史原因,有些前面的
  这些golden test suite都没有测试连通性
  的实验,所以有些是有,有些是没有,这两种
  你都应该可以跑,有的你就跑,没有的就直
  接略过。


• 对，这个规则必须加上，而且要做成兼容旧
  资产的模式，不能因为老 suite 没有 Pre-
  Stage2 就把它们跑坏。

  我建议正式规则是：

  兼容原则

  - 新 suite：支持 Pre-Stage2
    Connectivity
  - 老 suite：没有这层也能正常跑
  - 有就执行，没有就跳过，不报错

  执行语义
  AEL 在跑 suite 时先检查：

  1. 这个 DUT / pack 是否声明了
     pre_stage2_connectivity
  2. 如果声明了，就按顺序执行
  3. 如果没声明，就直接进入原来的 Stage
     2
  4. 输出里明确写：
      - Pre-Stage2: 6 tests
      - 或 Pre-Stage2: not defined,
        skipped

  这样不会破坏历史 pack。

  我建议的落地模型
  给 pack 增加一个可选段，而不是强制改所
  有历史 stage 结构，比如：

  - pre_stage2_connectivity: [...]

  这样：

  - 新 pack 可以写
  - 老 pack 不需要动
  - runner 里判断字段是否存在即可

  运行策略

  - 存在且有内容：执行
  - 不存在：跳过
  - 存在但空：显示 defined but empty
  - 失败时默认阻断后续 Stage 2
  - 但允许 --force-after-connectivity-
    fail 这类显式 override

  对历史 suite 的处理
  分三类：

  1. 已有 connectivity tests

  - 直接挂进 pre_stage2_connectivity

  2. 没有专门 connectivity tests，但已有
     可复用小 probe

  - 复用改名或薄封装后挂进去

  3. 完全没有

  - 先不补，保持 skip
  - 文档里说明：no auto connectivity
    coverage

  inventory / describe 输出也要区分
  对每个 suite 显示：

  - pre_stage2_connectivity: present
  - count: N

  或者：

  - pre_stage2_connectivity: none
  - policy: skipped

  这样用户一眼能看出：

  - 这套 suite 有没有前置连通性验证
  - 没有的话不是坏了，是历史原因未定义

  我建议的正式策略文案
  可以定成下面这个行为标准：

  - Connectivity prechecks are optional
    at schema level, mandatory when
    declared.
  - If a suite defines pre-stage2
    connectivity tests, AEL runs them
    before Stage 2 and blocks Stage 2 on
    failure by default.
  - If a suite does not define them, AEL
    skips the phase and proceeds without
    error.

  实现计划更新后应该是这样

  1. 先写设计文档

  - 定义 Pre-Stage2 Connectivity
  - 明确“可选声明、存在则必跑”的兼容规则

  2. 扩 runner

  - 支持可选 pre_stage2_connectivity

  选的 pre_stage2_connectivity，然后我会
  把 F103RCT6 这套先落地，再完整跑一遍。

    23 +#define ADC_SR_EOC      (1U << 1
        )
    24 +#define ADC_CR2_ADON    (1U << 0
        )
    25 +#define ADC_CR2_RSTCAL  (1U << 3
        )
    26 +#define ADC_CR2_CAL     (1U << 2
        )
    27 +#define ADC_CR2_EXTTRIG (1U << 2
        0)
    28 +#define ADC_CR2_SWSTART (1U << 2
        2)
    29 +
    30 +#define HIGH_MIN 2500u
    31 +#define LOW_MAX  900u
    32 +
    33 +static void delay(uint32_t n)
    34 +{
    35 +    while (n--) __asm__ volatile
         ("nop");
    36 +}
    37 +
    38 +static uint32_t adc_read(void)
    39 +{
    40 +    ADC1_SR &= ~ADC_SR_EOC;
    41 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_SWSTART;
    42 +    for (volatile uint32_t t = 4
        00000u; (ADC1_SR & ADC_SR_EOC) =
        = 0u && t > 0u; t--) {
    43 +    }
    44 +    return ADC1_DR & 0xFFFu;
    45 +}
    46 +
    47 +int main(void)
    48 +{
    49 +    RCC_CFGR &= ~(3u << 14);
    50 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= (1u << 2) | (
        1u << 9);
    51 +
    52 +    GPIOA_CRL &= ~0xFFu;
    53 +    GPIOA_CRL |= 0x03u;
    54 +    GPIOA_ODR &= ~(1u << 0u);
    55 +
    56 +    ADC1_CR1 = 0u;
    57 +    ADC1_CR2 = ADC_CR2_ADON | (7
        u << 17) | ADC_CR2_EXTTRIG;
    58 +    ADC1_SMPR2 = (7u << 3);
    59 +    ADC1_SQR1 = 0u;
    60 +    ADC1_SQR3 = 1u;
    61 +
    62 +    for (volatile uint32_t i = 0
        ; i < 200u; i++) {
    63 +        __asm__ volatile ("nop")
        ;
    64 +    }
    65 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_RSTCAL;
    66 +    while (ADC1_CR2 & ADC_CR2_RS
        TCAL) {}
    67 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_CAL;
    68 +    while (ADC1_CR2 & ADC_CR2_CA
        L) {}
    69 +
    70 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    71 +
    72 +    GPIOA_ODR |= (1u << 0u);
    73 +    delay(4000u);
    74 +    {
    75 +        uint32_t high = adc_read
        ();
    76 +        if (high < HIGH_MIN) {
    77 +            ael_mailbox_fail(0xE
        401u, high);
    78 +            while (1) {}
    79 +        }
    80 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (
        high << 16u);
    81 +    }
    82 +
    83 +    GPIOA_ODR &= ~(1u << 0u);
    84 +    delay(4000u);
    85 +    {
    86 +        uint32_t low = adc_read(
        );
    87 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 |=
        low;
    88 +        if (low > LOW_MAX) {
    89 +            ael_mailbox_fail(0xE
        402u, AEL_MAILBOX->detail0);
    90 +            while (1) {}
    91 +        }
    92 +    }
    93 +
    94 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    95 +    while (1) {
    96 +        delay(12000u);
    97 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    98 +    }
    99 +}

    28 +    uint32_t low_seen = 0u;

    52 +                while (1) {}
    53 +            }
    54 +            high_seen++;
    55 +        } else {
    56 +            if (GPIOB_IDR & (1u
        << 1u)) {
    57 +                ael_mailbox_fail

        ) | low_seen);
    58 +                while (1) {}
    59 +            }
    60 +            low_seen++;
    61 +        }

        high_seen << 16u) | low_seen;
    64 +        if (high_seen >= 4u && l

    65 +            ael_mailbox_pass();
    66 +            while (1) {
    67 +                if ((SYST_CSR &
        SYST_CSR_COUNTFLAG) == 0u) {
    68 +                    continue;
    69 +                }
    70 +                AEL_MAILBOX->det
        ail0++;
    71 +            }
    72 +        }
    73 +    }

• 我已经定位到根因了：flash_bmda_gdbmi
  只要看到 127.0.0.1:gdb_port，就默认要
  去 bootstrap 一个本地 ST-Link server。

  是错的。我准备直接在 flash adapter 里
  加一个分支，让 daplink 走“外部 GDB
  server 已经存在”的路径。

      1 +# STM32F103RCT6 Golden Suite Pre-Stage2 Closeout
      2 +
      3 +Date: 2026-03-31
      4 +
      5 +## Outcome
      6 +
      7 +`STM32F103RCT6` now includes an explicit `pre_stage2_connectivity` layer in its canonical golden pack:
      8 +
      9 +- pack: `packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json`
     10 +- board: `stm32f103rct6`
     11 +- control instrument: `daplink_f103_rct6`
     12 +- transport: local `DAPLink + OpenOCD gdb_remote`
     13 +
     14 +The canonical pack completed live validation with `20/20 PASS`.
     15 +
     16 +Primary evidence:
     17 +
     18 +- pack result: `pack_runs/2026-03-31_08-15-39_stm32f103rct6_golden_stm32f103rct6/pack_result.json`
     19 +
     20 +## Pre-Stage2 Connectivity Coverage
     21 +
     22 +The new `pre_stage2_connectivity` section proves the current bench wiring before Stage 2 feature tests run:
     23 +
     24 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb0_pb1_probe`
     25 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe`
     26 +- `stm32f103rct6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe`
     27 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb15_pb14_probe`
     28 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_tx_probe`
     29 +
     30 +This layer validates:
     31 +
     32 +- digital GPIO jumper continuity on `PB0 <-> PB1`
     33 +- timer/PWM jumper continuity on `PB8 <-> PB9`
     34 +- analog loop path on `PA0 <-> PA1`
     35 +- SPI jumper continuity on `PB15 <-> PB14`
     36 +- host-observed UART TX path on `PA9 -> DAPLink RX`
     37 +
     38 +Current canonical fixture:
     39 +
     40 +- `DAPLink SWD`
     41 +- `DAPLink UART <-> PA9/PA10`
     42 +- `PC8 <-> PC9`
     43 +- `PB0 <-> PB1`
     44 +- `PB8 <-> PB9`
     45 +- `PA0 <-> PA1`
     46 +- `PB15 <-> PB14`
     47 +
     48 +## Final Suite Shape
     49 +
     50 +Stage 0:
     51 +
     52 +- `stm32f103rct6_pc8_pc9_probe`
     53 +- `stm32f103rct6_minimal_runtime_mailbox`
     54 +
     55 +Stage 1:
     56 +
     57 +- `stm32f103rct6_timer_mailbox`
     58 +- `stm32f103rct6_systick_mailbox`
     59 +- `stm32f103rct6_internal_temp_mailbox`
     60 +
     61 +Pre-Stage2 Connectivity:
     62 +
     63 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb0_pb1_probe`
     64 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe`
     65 +- `stm32f103rct6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe`
     66 +- `stm32f103rct6_pb15_pb14_probe`
     67 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_tx_probe`
     68 +
     69 +Stage 2:
     70 +
     71 +- `stm32f103rct6_gpio_loopback`
     72 +- `stm32f103rct6_exti_trigger`
     73 +- `stm32f103rct6_adc_loopback`
     74 +- `stm32f103rct6_spi_loopback`
     75 +- `stm32f103rct6_iwdg`
     76 +- `stm32f103rct6_capture_mailbox`
     77 +- `stm32f103rct6_pwm_capture`
     78 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_multibyte`
     79 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_dma`
     80 +
     81 +Stage 3:
     82 +
     83 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_banner`
     84 +
     85 +## Important Implementation Notes
     86 +
     87 +- `pre_stage2_connectivity` is optional at pack level.
     88 +- If a pack defines it, `ael pack` now runs it before Stage 2.
     89 +- If a historical pack does not define it, AEL skips it without error.
     90 +- `stm32f103rct6_uart_banner` was converted to a UART-only proof because this DAPLink fixture does not expose a separate logic-analyzer verify p
in.
     91 +- Local `DAPLink + OpenOCD` runs required host-level execution. Sandbox-local pack runs could build successfully but failed to use the localhost
 GDB server.
     92 +
     93 +## Residual Limits
     94 +
     95 +Still not auto-proven in the current canonical fixture:
     96 +
     97 +- UART RX host-to-target path as a dedicated pre-stage2 probe
     98 +- visual LED behavior on `PC7`
     99 +- features that require extra external hardware, including `I2C`, `USB`, and `CAN`
    100 +
    101 +These are known limits, not regressions in the canonical suite.

• Added docs/skills/stm32_pre_stage2_connectivity_with_daplink_2026-03-31.md (+79 -0)
     1 +# STM32 Pre-Stage2 Connectivity With DAPLink
     2 +
     3 +Date: 2026-03-31
     4 +
     5 +## When To Use
     6 +
     7 +Use this pattern when:
     8 +
     9 +- a canonical STM32 golden suite runs on local `DAPLink + OpenOCD`
    10 +- Stage 2 depends on jumper continuity
    11 +- you want to fail early on wiring faults instead of misclassifying them as feature failures
    12 +
    13 +## Core Rule
    14 +
    15 +If a pack defines `pre_stage2_connectivity`, run those tests before Stage 2.
    16 +
    17 +If a historical pack does not define it, skip it without error.
    18 +
    19 +## Recommended Probe Types
    20 +
    21 +Prefer small mailbox or observed-UART probes that only prove connectivity:
    22 +
    23 +- digital jumper probe
    24 +- analog threshold probe
    25 +- timer-edge jumper probe
    26 +- UART TX observed probe
    27 +
    28 +Avoid mixing connectivity proof with richer feature semantics in this layer.
    29 +
    30 +## Reference Mapping
    31 +
    32 +`STM32F103RCT6` reference implementation:
    33 +
    34 +- `PB0 <-> PB1` -> `stm32f103rct6_pb0_pb1_probe`
    35 +- `PB8 <-> PB9` -> `stm32f103rct6_pb8_pb9_probe`
    36 +- `PA0 <-> PA1` -> `stm32f103rct6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe`
    37 +- `PB15 <-> PB14` -> `stm32f103rct6_pb15_pb14_probe`
    38 +- `PA9 -> DAPLink RX` -> `stm32f103rct6_uart_tx_probe`
    39 +
    40 +Pack reference:
    41 +
    42 +- `packs/stm32f103rct6_golden.json`
    43 +
    44 +## DAPLink / OpenOCD Execution Rule
    45 +
    46 +For local `DAPLink + OpenOCD` fixtures, full live pack runs must use host execution rather than sandbox-local execution.
    47 +
    48 +Reason:
    49 +
    50 +- sandbox-local runs may build successfully
    51 +- but the local GDB client can fail to attach to the host OpenOCD server even when the probe and target are healthy
    52 +
    53 +Working pattern:
    54 +
    55 +1. start `OpenOCD` on the host
    56 +2. point the board/instrument at the local `gdb_remote`
    57 +3. run `ael pack` on the host
    58 +
    59 +## UART Banner Rule
    60 +
    61 +If the fixture does not expose a separate logic-analyzer verify pin, convert banner proofs to UART-only observed tests.
    62 +
    63 +Do not keep stale `pin: "sig"` checks on a serial-only DAPLink fixture.
    64 +
    65 +## Practical Lesson
    66 +
    67 +`Pre-Stage2` should answer:
    68 +
    69 +- is the wire there
    70 +- is the host serial path alive
    71 +- is the loop path electrically present
    72 +
    73 +It should not answer:
    74 +
    75 +- is the peripheral perfectly characterized
    76 +- is timing accurate beyond coarse acceptance
    77 +- is the visual LED behavior correct
    78 +
    79 +This separation makes Stage 2 failures easier to trust.

  - stm32f103rct6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe
  - stm32f103rct6_pb15_pb14_probe
  - stm32f103rct6_uart_tx_probe

  兼容规则也已经落下来了：

  - 新 pack 如果定义了 pre_stage2_connectivity，AEL 会在 Stage 2 前先跑
  - 老 pack 如果没有定义，会直接跳过，不报错

  另外我把 stm32f103rct6_uart_banner 改成了适合当前 DAPLink fixture 的 UART-only proof，去掉了不成立的 sig 观察要求；同时修了本地 DAPLink + OpenOCD 路径
，避免它误走 ST-Link bootstrap。最终 inventory 现在会显示：

  - suite_tier: canonical_golden
  - pre_stage2_connectivity_count: 5

› stm32f103rct6 for this, give me a
  plan.How you will fix it, migrate it


• Plan

  对 STM32F103RCT6，我会把“修好并迁移到
  标准形态”拆成 6 步。现在其实大部分已经
  完成了，下面这套也是后续同类板子的标准
  迁移模板。

  1. 固定 canonical identity
  先只保留一条正式路径，不再混用历史入
  口：

  - canonical board: stm32f103rct6
  - canonical pack: packs/
    stm32f103rct6_golden.json
  - canonical instrument:
    daplink_f103_rct6
  - canonical transport: DAPLink + local
    OpenOCD gdb_remote
  - canonical wiring:
      - DAPLink SWD
      - DAPLink UART <-> PA9/PA10
      - PC8 <-> PC9
      - PB0 <-> PB1
      - PB8 <-> PB9
      - PA0 <-> PA1
      - PB15 <-> PB14

  这一步的目标是：以后用户问
  STM32F103RCT6，只返回这一条正式路径。

  2. 把连通性从“隐含前提”变成正式层
  在 Stage 2 前加
  pre_stage2_connectivity，先证明线是通
  的，再跑 feature tests。

  当前这层应包括：

  - pb0_pb1_probe
  - pb8_pb9_probe
  - pa0_pa1_adc_probe
  - pb15_pb14_probe
  - uart_tx_probe

  策略是：

  - 有定义就先跑
  - 失败默认阻断 Stage 2
  - 老 suite 没有这层就直接跳过，不报错

  这一步的目标是：把“接线问题”和“功能问
  题”分离开。

  3. 清理不适合当前 fixture 的旧验证方式
  重点是去掉和当前 DAPLink fixture 不匹
  配的历史假设。

  比如：

  - uart_banner 不再要求不存在的 sig 观
    察线
  - 改成纯 UART-observed proof
  - PC7 LED 不再作为 canonical 机器验证
    路径
  - 用 PC8 <-> PC9 probe 替代 visual-
    only 依赖

  这一步的目标是：所有通过都是真正由当前
  bench 证明的，不靠历史残留配置碰运气。

  4. 修正运行链路，让 DAPLink 真正成为正
  式入口
  这里要修两类问题：

  - inventory / board / instrument
    metadata 正确指向 daplink_f103_rct6
  - flash/runtime adapter 不再把本地
    DAPLink + OpenOCD 错当成 ST-Link
    bootstrap

  具体原则：

  - DAPLink 走外部已存在的 OpenOCD
    gdb_remote
  - 不再先跑 st-info --probe
  - full live run 用 host execution，不
    走受限 sandbox

  这一步的目标是：让 suite runner 和真实
  硬件路径一致。

  5. 跑 full pack，拿到唯一有效完成信号
  必须跑完整 pack，不只看单测。

  对 STM32F103RCT6，目标就是：

  - 20/20 PASS



















› That's very good.Follow this plan.Go
  ahead implement it

  canonical wiring、pre-stage2 覆盖范围
  和未自动覆盖项正式挂到资产里，而不是只
  留在 closeout 里。

› why? 当前唯一没提交的是自动更新文件：

    - ael/civilization/data/run_index.json


• 因为它不是这次任务的源码或配置改动，而是 运行过程中自动累积的运行历史数据。

  具体说，ael/civilization/data/run_index.json 会在你每次：

  - 跑 test
  - 跑 pack
  - 做 live validation

  时自动变化，里面记录的是 run history、统计和经验索引。它更像：

  - runtime cache
  - generated state
  - local evidence index

  而不是这次我手工实现的功能代码。

  我没把它提交进去，主要有三个原因：

  1. 它不是原子 intent 的一部分
     你让我做的是：

  - 加 pre-stage2 connectivity
  - 跑完整 suite
  - 补 closeout / skill
    run_index.json 只是这些动作附带产生的状态文件，不是功能实现本身。

  2. 它很容易产生无意义噪音
     这个文件会随着每次跑测不断变化。把它混进功能 commit，会让 commit 不干净，也不利于 review。
  3. 项目里这类文件通常不适合跟功能代码一起绑定
     除非你明确希望“把这次新增的 CE 记录和 run index 一起固化到仓库”，否则更稳妥的做法就是不提交它。

  一句话说：
  我不提交它，是为了保持 commit 干净，避免把自动生成的运行状态和真正的实现改动混在一起。

  如果你希望，我也可以单独把它作为一个“更新 CE/runtime index”的独立 commit 提交，但我默认不这么做。


› then maybe add it to .gitignores?


• 我先检查 .gitignore 里对 ael/civilization/data/run_index.json 的处理，再决定是加精确忽略规则，还是用更合适的 generated-state 模式收口。

• .gitignore 里现在没有这条规则。我会先把 ael/civilization/data/run_index.json 明确标成 generated runtime state；但要说明一点：因为它已经被 Git 跟踪了，
单加 .gitignore 只能防止以后新文件被纳入，不能让这个已跟踪文件自动安静下来。

• 加了，并已提交：

  - ddb57de chore: ignore civilization run index

  不过要注意一件关键事：

  - ael/civilization/data/run_index.json 已经是被 Git 跟踪的文件
  - 所以单独加 .gitignore 之后，它仍然会继续显示修改
  - .gitignore 只会影响“未被跟踪的新文件”

  如果你想让它以后彻底不再出现在 git status，还需要再做一步：

  - git rm --cached ael/civilization/data/run_index.json

  我这次没直接做这一步，因为那属于改变 Git 跟踪状态，不该在你没明确要求时自动做。
  如果你要，我下一步可以把它从版本控制里移除并单独提交一个原子 commit。


› 那我建议你撤销刚才的更改,还是我们要用git继续跟踪这个文件。等将来它变得太大了,比如说,我们再继续处理,现在还是作为一个可跟踪的文件,不要ignore它。
